Allah's Transcendence Above Change and States
Maturidi proves Allah's transcendence above change and states.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah is not subject to change or contingent states, and why attributing such to Him would compromise His oneness and eternity.

Core Idea
Allah is beyond all change; states are contingent and cannot apply to the Eternal.

Maturidi begins by explaining that Allah's essence is existence pure and simple, without non-existence. He then argues that Allah has never changed nor will change, because change would imply that He is affected by states, which are created and contingent. Accepting that would destroy the very foundations of tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on al-huwiyya and changelessness
Read the Arabic passage once, focusing on the definition of al-huwiyya and the statement that Allah is without change or transition.
The passage uses a series of negations: bighair taghayyur, zawal, intiqal...
2
Understand the argument against states (ahwal)
Analyze why Maturidi says that if states vary upon Allah, He would be described by temporality, leading to the fall of oneness and eternity.
The key phrase: 'wa man la yufariq al-ahwal, wa hunna ahadath, yajibu biha al-wasf bi al-ahdath'.
3
Connect the argument to tawhid
Reflect on how attributing change to Allah would make Him dependent on something else (al-ghayr), thus negating His self-sufficiency and unity.
The conclusion: 'fathabata bi dhalika al-ghayr, li taghayyur al-ahwal 'alayh'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الهوية في الشاهد كناية عن الوجود، وتأويله نفي العدم عنه. والله تعالى لم يزل ولا يزال بلا تغير ولا زوال ولا انتقال من حال إلى حال ولا تحرك ولا قرار. إذ هو وصف اختلاف تختلف الأحوال عليه فهو غير مفارق لها؛ ومن لا يفارق الأحوال، وهن أحداث، يجب بها الوصف بالأحداث. وفي ذلك سقوط الوحدانية ثم القدم، ثم جرى الأحوال، ومن تدبير الغير عليه؛ إذ حال من الأحوال لو كانت لذاته لم يجز تغيرها ما دامت ذاته. فثبت بذلك الغير، لتغير الأحوال عليه وتنقله من حال إلى حال. وذلك دليل تعاليه عن الوصف بالمكان؛ إذ قد ثبت أن قد كان ولا مكان. وليس في الإضافة إلى أنه على العرش استوى تثبيت مكان، كما لم يكن في قوله: ونحن أقرب إليه من حبل الوريد، وقوله: ما يكون من نجوى ثلاثة إلا هو رابعهم، وقوله: ونحن أقرب إليه منكم ذلك. على أن القول بالمكان ليس من نوع التعظيم والتبجيل. بل الأمكنة إنما شرفت به، وتفاوتت أقدارها بتفضيله مكانًا على مكان بجعله مخصوصا لأخيار خلقه أو لما جعل لعبادته وتعظيمه فيه. فأما أن يكون أحد تعلو رتبته بالمكان من ملوك الأرض أو الأخيار فليس بممكن، فكيف بالملك الجبار الذي ما ارتفع قدر مكان ولا جل خطره إلا به؟ وإذا كان كذلك بطل أن يكون في الإضافة تعظيمه. ثم يكون فيما بعد ذلك للحاجة، وهو يتعالى عنها. فلذلك لم يجب بقوله: الرحمن على العرش استوى معنى الكون في المكان؛ إذ ذلك الحرف يعبر به عن العلو والجلال ومحال مثله له بخلقه. فثبت أن ذلك من الوجه الذي يستحقه بذاته من العلو والرفعة وما هو بذاته عليه، فهو كان كذلك ولا خلق، لم يجز الوصف له بالخلق. ولا قوة إلا بالله. ما يكون ذلك الاعتقاد عن علم تقدم بحال من يضاف إليه ذلك في الشاهد قبل الإضافة من الاحتمال. ثم الله سبحانه كان ولا مكان، وعلى ذلك اعتقد الأنام. لم يجز أن
Then identity (al-huwiyya) in the witnessed world is a metaphor for existence, and its interpretation is negation of non-existence from Him. And Allah, exalted, has not ceased and will not cease without change, passing away, transition from state to state, movement, or rest. For it is a description of difference — states vary upon Him and He is not separate from them; and whoever is not separate from states, and they are events, must be described by events. And in that is the fall of oneness and then eternity, then the management of the other would occur upon Him; for if a state among states were inherent in His essence, its change would not be permissible as long as His essence endures. So by that, the other is established, because of the change of states upon Him and His transition from state to state. And that is evidence of His transcendence above description by place; for it has been established that He was and no place was. And there is not in the attribution that He established Himself over the Throne a confirmation of place, just as there is not in His saying: 'And We are closer to him than the jugular vein' and His saying: 'There is no secret conversation of three except that He is their fourth' and His saying: 'And We are closer to him than you' that. Moreover, the statement about place is not a type of glorification and magnification. Rather, places are only honored by Him, and their values vary by His preference of one place over another by making it specific for His chosen creation or for what He made for His worship and glorification in it. But that anyone should be elevated in rank by place — from the kings of the earth or the righteous — is not possible, so how about the Almighty King whose rank no place has elevated and whose status no place has magnified except through Him? And if it is so, then in the attribution [of place to Him] glorification is nullified. Then after that it would be for need, and He is exalted above it. Therefore, from His saying: 'The Most Merciful established Himself over the Throne' the meaning of being in a place is not intended; for that letter is used for exaltation and majesty, and it is impossible for Him to be similar to His creation. So it is established that it is from the aspect that He deserves by His essence of exaltation and highness and what He is upon by His essence; for He was such and no creation, it is not permissible to describe Him with creation. And there is no power except through Allah. Such belief cannot be based on knowledge preceded by a state of one to whom that is attributed in the witnessed world before the attribution, due to probability. Then Allah, exalted, was and no place was, and upon that the people have believed. It is not permissible that...
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a complex argument combining two closely related doctrinal points: Allah's transcendence above change and above place. Maturidi begins by explaining 'identity' (al-huwiyya) as existential reality without non-existence. He then argues that Allah is not subject to change, because change would imply that states (ahwal) affect Him, and since states are contingent, attributing them to Allah would compromise His oneness and eternity. Moreover, if states were part of His essence, they could not change; but change is observed in the world, so the changer is other than Allah. This very argument proves that Allah is not in any place, because He existed before any place existed. He then addresses the Qur'anic verses that might suggest spatial location, such as 'He established Himself over the Throne'. Maturidi argues that such expressions do not affirm place, just as verses about closeness do not imply physical proximity. He further explains that places are honored by Allah, not that Allah is honored by a place. If a place's honor comes from Him, then He cannot be in need of it. The term 'istawa' (established) is interpreted as expressing exaltation and majesty, not physical location. The lesson ends with a note that true belief in Allah's transcendence is based on knowledge that He was without place, as the early community believed.

Key Terms

Allah's Transcendence Above Place and the Meaning of Istiwa'
Maturidi proves Allah's transcendence above place and interprets istiwa' as exaltation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Allah cannot be in a place and how verses like 'Istiwa over the Throne' are interpreted as exaltation, not physical location.

Core Idea
Allah is beyond place; His existence preceded all places.

Maturidi continues by showing that the same reasoning that negates change also negates place for Allah. He then addresses the apparent difficulty of verses that seem to imply spatial location, such as 'al-Rahman 'ala al-'arsh istawa', explaining that this means absolute exaltation and authority, not sitting.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument against place
Read the Arabic passage that begins with 'wa dhalika dalil ta'aliyhi 'an al-wasf bi al-makan' and understand the logical connection to the previous argument.

ثم الهوية في الشاهد كناية عن الوجود، وتأويله نفي العدم عنه. والله تعالى لم يزل ولا يزال بلا تغير ولا زوال ولا انتقال من حال إلى حال ولا تحرك ولا قرار. إذ هو وصف اختلاف تختلف الأحوال عليه فهو غير مفارق لها؛ ومن لا يفارق الأحوال، وهن أحداث، يجب بها الوصف بالأحداث. وفي ذلك سقوط الوحدانية ثم القدم، ثم جرى الأحوال، ومن تدبير الغير عليه؛ إذ حال من الأحوال لو كانت لذاته لم يجز تغيرها ما دامت ذاته. فثبت بذلك الغير، لتغير الأحوال عليه وتنقله من حال إلى حال. وذلك دليل تعاليه عن الوصف بالمكان؛ إذ قد ثبت أن قد كان ولا مكان. وليس في الإضافة إلى أنه على العرش استوى تثبيت مكان، كما لم يكن في قوله: ونحن أقرب إليه من حبل الوريد، وقوله: ما يكون من نجوى ثلاثة إلا هو رابعهم، وقوله: ونحن أقرب إليه منكم ذلك. على أن القول بالمكان ليس من نوع التعظيم والتبجيل. بل الأمكنة إنما شرفت به، وتفاوتت أقدارها بتفضيله مكانًا على مكان بجعله مخصوصا لأخيار خلقه أو لما جعل لعبادته وتعظيمه فيه. فأما أن يكون أحد تعلو رتبته بالمكان من ملوك الأرض أو الأخيار فليس بممكن، فكيف بالملك الجبار الذي ما ارتفع قدر مكان ولا جل خطره إلا به؟ وإذا كان كذلك بطل أن يكون في الإضافة تعظيمه. ثم يكون فيما بعد ذلك للحاجة، وهو يتعالى عنها. فلذلك لم يجب بقوله: الرحمن على العرش استوى معنى الكون في المكان؛ إذ ذلك الحرف يعبر به عن العلو والجلال ومحال مثله له بخلقه. فثبت أن ذلك من الوجه الذي يستحقه بذاته من العلو والرفعة وما هو بذاته عليه، فهو كان كذلك ولا خلق، لم يجز الوصف له بالخلق. ولا قوة إلا بالله. ما يكون ذلك الاعتقاد عن علم تقدم بحال من يضاف إليه ذلك في الشاهد قبل الإضافة من الاحتمال. ثم الله سبحانه كان ولا مكان، وعلى ذلك اعتقد الأنام. لم يجز أن
Then identity (al-huwiyya) in the witnessed world is a metaphor for existence, and its interpretation is negation of non-existence from Him. And Allah, exalted, has not ceased and will not cease without change, passing away, transition from state to state, movement, or rest. For it is a description of difference — states vary upon Him and He is not separate from them; and whoever is not separate from states, and they are events, must be described by events. And in that is the fall of oneness and then eternity, then the management of the other would occur upon Him; for if a state among states were inherent in His essence, its change would not be permissible as long as His essence endures. So by that, the other is established, because of the change of states upon Him and His transition from state to state. And that is evidence of His transcendence above description by place; for it has been established that He was and no place was. And there is not in the attribution that He established Himself over the Throne a confirmation of place, just as there is not in His saying: 'And We are closer to him than the jugular vein' and His saying: 'There is no secret conversation of three except that He is their fourth' and His saying: 'And We are closer to him than you' that. Moreover, the statement about place is not a type of glorification and magnification. Rather, places are only honored by Him, and their values vary by His preference of one place over another by making it specific for His chosen creation or for what He made for His worship and glorification in it. But that anyone should be elevated in rank by place — from the kings of the earth or the righteous — is not possible, so how about the Almighty King whose rank no place has elevated and whose status no place has magnified except through Him? And if it is so, then in the attribution [of place to Him] glorification is nullified. Then after that it would be for need, and He is exalted above it. Therefore, from His saying: 'The Most Merciful established Himself over the Throne' the meaning of being in a place is not intended; for that letter is used for exaltation and majesty, and it is impossible for Him to be similar to His creation. So it is established that it is from the aspect that He deserves by His essence of exaltation and highness and what He is upon by His essence; for He was such and no creation, it is not permissible to describe Him with creation. And there is no power except through Allah. Such belief cannot be based on knowledge preceded by a state of one to whom that is attributed in the witnessed world before the attribution, due to probability. Then Allah, exalted, was and no place was, and upon that the people have believed. It is not permissible that...
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a complex argument combining two closely related doctrinal points: Allah's transcendence above change and above place. Maturidi begins by explaining 'identity' (al-huwiyya) as existential reality without non-existence. He then argues that Allah is not subject to change, because change would imply that states (ahwal) affect Him, and since states are contingent, attributing them to Allah would compromise His oneness and eternity. Moreover, if states were part of His essence, they could not change; but change is observed in the world, so the changer is other than Allah. This very argument proves that Allah is not in any place, because He existed before any place existed. He then addresses the Qur'anic verses that might suggest spatial location, such as 'He established Himself over the Throne'. Maturidi argues that such expressions do not affirm place, just as verses about closeness do not imply physical proximity. He further explains that places are honored by Allah, not that Allah is honored by a place. If a place's honor comes from Him, then He cannot be in need of it. The term 'istawa' (established) is interpreted as expressing exaltation and majesty, not physical location. The lesson ends with a note that true belief in Allah's transcendence is based on knowledge that He was without place, as the early community believed.

Key Terms
المكان
العرش
الاستواء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah sits physically on the Throne in a spatial sense.
Correction: Maturidi explains that 'istiwa' indicates absolute exaltation and authority, not physical location, and that Allah is beyond place altogether.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does 'al-Rahman 'ala al-'arsh istawa' mean?
A) Allah sits on the Throne as a king sits on a throne
B) Allah is located upward in the direction of the Throne
C) It expresses Allah's absolute exaltation and majesty, not physical location
D) The Throne holds Allah's divine presence

Key Takeaway
Allah is not confined to any place; His acts of 'istiwa' are expressions of His supreme authority and exaltation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you close your eyes to pray, do you unconsciously locate Allah somewhere like the heavens? How does this lesson’s truth—that He was when there was no place—reshape your awareness of His presence in every moment?

?
If places are only honored because of Him, then what about the place of your heart? Is it a place where He is honored, or is it filled with distractions that make Him remote? What step will you take this hour to make your heart a place worthy of His presence?

The Impermissibility of Describing Allah with Place and the Meaning of Istawa
Maturidi refutes place attribution and interprets istawa as transcendence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why describing Allah with place is impermissible and how to correctly interpret the verse 'al-Rahman 'ala al-'arsh istawa.'

Core Idea
Allah existed before place; describing Him with place imposes limitation.

Maturidi begins by stating the ruling that Allah cannot be described with place. He then provides the rational proof that since Allah existed before any place, describing Him with place would imply change. He also refutes the literalist interpretation of istawa, showing that such verses use the language of highness and majesty, not physical location. This lesson establishes the foundational principle of divine transcendence over place.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Maturidi uses a very logical, argumentative style.
2
Identify the key proof
Find the statement that Allah was and there was no place. This is the central rational proof that place cannot be attributed to Him.
3
Understand the refutation of literal istawa
Maturidi argues that the expression 'istawa' is used for highness and majesty, not physical location. See how he compares it to other Quranic verses like 'We are nearer to him than the jugular vein.'
4
Appreciate the distinction between glorification of place vs. glorification of Allah
Maturidi shows that places are honored by Allah, not the other way around. Attributing place to Allah would imply need, which is impossible for Him.
5

وذلك دليل تعاليه عن الوصف بالمكان؛ إذ قد ثبت أن قد كان ولا مكان. وليس في الإضافة إلى أنه على العرش استوى تثبيت مكان، كما لم يكن في قوله: ونحن أقرب إليه من حبل الوريد، وقوله: ما يكون من نجوى ثلاثة إلا هو رابعهم، وقوله: ونحن أقرب إليه منكم ذلك. على أن القول بالمكان ليس من نوع التعظيم والتبجيل. بل الأمكنة إنما شرفت به، وتفاوتت أقدارها بتفضيله مكانًا على مكان بجعله مخصوصا لأخيار خلقه أو لما جعل لعبادته وتعظيمه فيه. فأما أن يكون أحد تعلو رتبته بالمكان من ملوك الأرض أو الأخيار فليس بممكن، فكيف بالملك الجبار الذي ما ارتفع قدر مكان ولا جل خطره إلا به؟ وإذا كان كذلك بطل أن يكون في الإضافة تعظيمه. ثم يكون فيما بعد ذلك للحاجة، وهو يتعالى عنها. فلذلك لم يجب بقوله: الرحمن على العرش استوى معنى الكون في المكان؛ إذ ذلك الحرف يعبر به عن العلو والجلال ومحال مثله له بخلقه. فثبت أن ذلك من الوجه الذي يستحقه بذاته من العلو والرفعة وما هو بذاته عليه، فهو كان كذلك ولا خلق، لم يجز الوصف له بالخلق. ولا قوة إلا بالله.

يتغير الفهم عن الإضافة عما كان من قبل، وإليه ينصرف الفهم عن الإضافة إلى خلقه. على أن تخصيص إضافات الأشياء إلى الله في الشاهد يخرج مخرج التعظيم لها بما جعل فيها من الأمور المرضية والأحوال المحمودة، فما بال العرش من بين ذلك؟ ولا قوة إلا بالله. وعلى ذلك يفسد قول من يصفه بكل مكان؛ إذ لا فرق بين مكان واحد مخصوص يضاف إليه وبين الجملة. بل الفرد في بيان تعظيمه أولى؛ إذ في ذلك تخصيص ذلك الشيء بالذكر، وفي الذكر تشريف وتكريم؛ فيرجع إلى ذكر علو ذلك الشيء. وفي الإرسال وجمع الكل يرجع إلى تخصيص حقيقة صفة الله. كما يقال: رب كل شيء، وإله كل شيء، على تعظيم الرب وتبجيله. وإذا قيل: رب محمد وإله إبراهيم، فإنما يقصد قصد تشريفهما وتعظيمهما. فقياس ذلك أن تكون الإضافة إلى العرش توجب تعظيم العرش وتكريمه، وإلى كل الأمكنة توجب وصف الله بها، وذلك قبيح؛ إذ لم يكن يوصف به في الأزل. ولا يوصف شيء بالقرب إلى الله من طريق المسافة والمساحة ولا هو بالقرب إلى شيء من ذلك الوجه؛ إذ ذلك جهة الحدود والتقدير بالأمكنة؛ وقد كان ولا مكان فهو على ما كان يتعالى عن الزمان والمكان؛ إذ إليهما ترجع حدود الأشياء ونهايتها. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
مسألة
نسبة الماهية والكيفية والقرب إلى الله تعالى
وقول الرجل قد يُكنى به عن اسمه، كقول فرعون: وما رب العالمين؟ قال: رب
The impermissibility of describing Him, exalted, with place. And that is a proof of His transcendence above description with place; for it has been established that He was and there was no place. And in the attribution that He 'established Himself upon the Throne' there is no affirmation of a place, just as there was not in His saying: 'And We are nearer to him than the jugular vein' (50:16), and His saying: 'There is no secret conversation of three except that He is the fourth of them' (58:7), and His saying: 'And We are nearer to him than you' (56:85) any of that. Moreover, the statement about place is not of the type of glorification and veneration. Rather, places only become honored by Him, and their ranks vary by His preferring one place over another by making it specific for His chosen servants or for what He made for His worship and veneration therein. As for that anyone's rank be elevated by place, among the kings of the earth or the righteous, that is not possible; how then about the King, the Compeller, whose rank no place elevates nor is its danger great except by Him? And if it is so, it becomes invalid that there be glorification in attribution (to place). Then it (attribution) would be for need, and He is exalted above it. Therefore, it is not required by His saying: 'The Most Merciful established Himself upon the Throne' (20:5) the meaning of being in place; for that expression is used to denote highness and majesty, and it is impossible for one like Him to have that for His creation. So it is established that that is from the aspect which He deserves by His essence of highness and elevation and what He is upon by His essence. He was thus without creation, and it is not permissible to describe Him with creation. And there is no power except with Allah. That belief is based on prior knowledge of the state of the one to whom that is attributed in the witnessed realm before the attribution of probability. Then Allah, glorified, was and there was no place, and upon that the people believe. It is not possible that the understanding of the attribution changes from what it was before, and to it the understanding of the attribution to His creation turns. Moreover, the specification of attributions of things to Allah in the witnessed realm takes the course of glorification for them because of what He placed in them of pleasing matters and praiseworthy states; so why the Throne in particular among that? And there is no power except with Allah. And upon that, the statement of the one who describes Him with every place is corrupted; for there is no difference between one specific place attributed to Him and the totality. Rather, the individual in expressing His glorification is more appropriate; for in that there is specification of that thing by mention, and in mention there is honor and veneration; so it returns to mentioning the highness of that thing. And in the general and the gathering of all, it returns to the specification of the reality of the attribute of Allah. As it is said: Lord of everything, and God of everything, upon the glorification and veneration of the Lord. And when it is said: Lord of Muhammad and God of Ibrahim, the intended purpose is only the honor and veneration of them both. So by analogy, the attribution to the Throne necessitates the glorification and honoring of the Throne, and to every place necessitates describing Allah with them, and that is repugnant; for He was not described with that in pre-eternity. And nothing is described as nearness to Allah by way of distance and measurement, nor is He near to anything by that way; for that is the domain of limits and estimation by places; and He was and there was no place, so He is as He was, exalted above time and place; for to them revert the limits and ends of things. And there is no power except with Allah. Issue: The relation of the essence, quality, and nearness to Allah, exalted. And the statement of a man may be used figuratively for his name, like the statement of Pharaoh: 'And what is the Lord of the worlds?' He said: 'Lord...'
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and explanation. It begins by stating the impermissibility of describing Allah with place, then provides a rational and scriptural proof. The author argues that since Allah existed before any place, describing Him with place is impossible. He refutes the literal interpretation of istawa (establishing upon the Throne) and similar verses, explaining that they do not imply physical location. He then shows that attributing place to Allah does not glorify Him; rather, places are glorified by Him. The argument proceeds to refute both the view that Allah is in a specific place (the Throne) and the view that He is everywhere, using the principle that such attributions would either limit Him or fail to properly honor Him. Finally, the passage introduces a new issue (mas'ala) about how to understand divine attributes like essence (mahiya), quality (kayfiyya), and nearness (qurb), emphasizing that these are not to be understood in a physical or spatial sense.

مكان
عرش
استوى
إضافة
تعظيم
أزل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Describing Allah with place is a form of glorification.
Correction: Places are glorified by Allah, not the other way around. Attributing place to Allah implies need and limitation, which is not glorification.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi argue that describing Allah with place is not glorification?
A) Because places are created and Allah is eternal.
B) Because places only become honored by Allah, not the other way around.
C) Because the Qur'an explicitly forbids it.
D) Because it implies Allah needs the place.

Key Takeaway
Allah existed before place and is transcendent above it; describing Him with place is impermissible and inconsistent with His majesty.

Understanding Divine Attributions: Why Allah is Neither in a Specific Place nor Everywhere
Maturidi refutes both specific and universal place attributions and clarifies divine nearness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how to correctly interpret divine attributions like nearness and establishment, and why it is equally wrong to say Allah is everywhere as it is to say He is in a specific place.

Core Idea
Attributing place to Allah limits His transcendence; He is exalted above both specific and universal location.

Maturidi continues his refutation by addressing how people might misunderstand divine attributions. He argues that when the Qur'an says 'We are nearer to him than the jugular vein,' it is not a spatial nearness but a divine awareness. He then refutes both the view that Allah is specifically on the Throne in a literal sense and the view that He is everywhere, showing that both fail to maintain His transcendence. This lesson clarifies the principle of divine transcendence over place in all its forms.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Maturidi uses examples from the Qur'an to support his argument.
2
Understand the principle of attribution
Maturidi explains that attributions like 'nearness' in the Qur'an are not spatial. They indicate divine knowledge and power, not physical proximity.
3
Refutation of the 'everywhere' view
See how Maturidi argues that saying Allah is everywhere is as problematic as saying He is in one specific place. Both imply limitation.
4
Appreciate the analogy with human honorifics
When we say 'Lord of Muhammad' it honors Muhammad, not God. Similarly, saying 'Lord of the Throne' honors the Throne, not God.
5
Solidify with the checkpoint
Answer the multiple-choice question to check your understanding.

عدم جواز وصفه تعالى بالمكان
وذلك دليل تعاليه عن الوصف بالمكان؛ إذ قد ثبت أن قد كان ولا مكان. وليس في الإضافة إلى أنه على العرش استوى تثبيت مكان، كما لم يكن في قوله: ونحن أقرب إليه من حبل الوريد، وقوله: ما يكون من نجوى ثلاثة إلا هو رابعهم، وقوله: ونحن أقرب إليه منكم ذلك. على أن القول بالمكان ليس من نوع التعظيم والتبجيل. بل الأمكنة إنما شرفت به، وتفاوتت أقدارها بتفضيله مكانًا على مكان بجعله مخصوصا لأخيار خلقه أو لما جعل لعبادته وتعظيمه فيه. فأما أن يكون أحد تعلو رتبته بالمكان من ملوك الأرض أو الأخيار فليس بممكن، فكيف بالملك الجبار الذي ما ارتفع قدر مكان ولا جل خطره إلا به؟ وإذا كان كذلك بطل أن يكون في الإضافة تعظيمه. ثم يكون فيما بعد ذلك للحاجة، وهو يتعالى عنها. فلذلك لم يجب بقوله: الرحمن على العرش استوى معنى الكون في المكان؛ إذ ذلك الحرف يعبر به عن العلو والجلال ومحال مثله له بخلقه. فثبت أن ذلك من الوجه الذي يستحقه بذاته من العلو والرفعة وما هو بذاته عليه، فهو كان كذلك ولا خلق، لم يجز الوصف له بالخلق. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
ما يكون ذلك الاعتقاد عن علم تقدم بحال من يضاف إليه ذلك في الشاهد قبل مع الإضافة من الاحتمال. ثم الله سبحانه كان ولا مكان، وعلى ذلك اعتقد الأنام. لم يجز أن
يتغير الفهم عن الإضافة عما كان من قبل، وإليه ينصرف الفهم عن الإضافة إلى خلقه. على أن تخصيص إضافات الأشياء إلى الله في الشاهد يخرج مخرج التعظيم لها بما جعل فيها من الأمور المرضية والأحوال المحمودة، فما بال العرش من بين ذلك؟ ولا قوة إلا بالله. وعلى ذلك يفسد قول من يصفه بكل مكان؛ إذ لا فرق بين مكان واحد مخصوص يضاف إليه وبين الجملة. بل الفرد في بيان تعظيمه أولى؛ إذ في ذلك تخصيص ذلك الشيء بالذكر، وفي الذكر تشريف وتكريم؛ فيرجع إلى ذكر علو ذلك الشيء. وفي الإرسال وجمع الكل يرجع إلى تخصيص حقيقة صفة الله. كما يقال: رب كل شيء، وإله كل شيء، على تعظيم الرب وتبجيله. وإذا قيل: رب محمد وإله إبراهيم، فإنما يقصد قصد تشريفهما وتعظيمهما. فقياس ذلك أن تكون الإضافة إلى العرش توجب تعظيم العرش وتكريمه، وإلى كل الأمكنة توجب وصف الله بها، وذلك قبيح؛ إذ لم يكن يوصف به في الأزل. ولا يوصف شيء بالقرب إلى الله من طريق المسافة والمساحة ولا هو بالقرب إلى شيء من ذلك الوجه؛ إذ ذلك جهة الحدود والتقدير بالأمكنة؛ وقد كان ولا مكان فهو على ما كان يتعالى عن الزمان والمكان؛ إذ إليهما ترجع حدود الأشياء ونهايتها. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
مسألة
نسبة الماهية والكيفية والقرب إلى الله تعالى
وقول الرجل قد يُكنى به عن اسمه، كقول فرعون: وما رب العالمين؟ قال: رب
The impermissibility of describing Him, exalted, with place. And that is a proof of His transcendence above description with place; for it has been established that He was and there was no place. And in the attribution that He 'established Himself upon the Throne' there is no affirmation of a place, just as there was not in His saying: 'And We are nearer to him than the jugular vein' (50:16), and His saying: 'There is no secret conversation of three except that He is the fourth of them' (58:7), and His saying: 'And We are nearer to him than you' (56:85) any of that. Moreover, the statement about place is not of the type of glorification and veneration. Rather, places only become honored by Him, and their ranks vary by His preferring one place over another by making it specific for His chosen servants or for what He made for His worship and veneration therein. As for that anyone's rank be elevated by place, among the kings of the earth or the righteous, that is not possible; how then about the King, the Compeller, whose rank no place elevates nor is its danger great except by Him? And if it is so, it becomes invalid that there be glorification in attribution (to place). Then it (attribution) would be for need, and He is exalted above it. Therefore, it is not required by His saying: 'The Most Merciful established Himself upon the Throne' (20:5) the meaning of being in place; for that expression is used to denote highness and majesty, and it is impossible for one like Him to have that for His creation. So it is established that that is from the aspect which He deserves by His essence of highness and elevation and what He is upon by His essence. He was thus without creation, and it is not permissible to describe Him with creation. And there is no power except with Allah. That belief is based on prior knowledge of the state of the one to whom that is attributed in the witnessed realm before the attribution of probability. Then Allah, glorified, was and there was no place, and upon that the people believe. It is not possible that the understanding of the attribution changes from what it was before, and to it the understanding of the attribution to His creation turns. Moreover, the specification of attributions of things to Allah in the witnessed realm takes the course of glorification for them because of what He placed in them of pleasing matters and praiseworthy states; so why the Throne in particular among that? And there is no power except with Allah. And upon that, the statement of the one who describes Him with every place is corrupted; for there is no difference between one specific place attributed to Him and the totality. Rather, the individual in expressing His glorification is more appropriate; for in that there is specification of that thing by mention, and in mention there is honor and veneration; so it returns to mentioning the highness of that thing. And in the general and the gathering of all, it returns to the specification of the reality of the attribute of Allah. As it is said: Lord of everything, and God of everything, upon the glorification and veneration of the Lord. And when it is said: Lord of Muhammad and God of Ibrahim, the intended purpose is only the honor and veneration of them both. So by analogy, the attribution to the Throne necessitates the glorification and honoring of the Throne, and to every place necessitates describing Allah with them, and that is repugnant; for He was not described with that in pre-eternity. And nothing is described as nearness to Allah by way of distance and measurement, nor is He near to anything by that way; for that is the domain of limits and estimation by places; and He was and there was no place, so He is as He was, exalted above time and place; for to them revert the limits and ends of things. And there is no power except with Allah. Issue: The relation of the essence, quality, and nearness to Allah, exalted. And the statement of a man may be used figuratively for his name, like the statement of Pharaoh: 'And what is the Lord of the worlds?' He said: 'Lord...'
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and explanation. It begins by stating the impermissibility of describing Allah with place, then provides a rational and scriptural proof. The author argues that since Allah existed before any place, describing Him with place is impossible. He refutes the literal interpretation of istawa (establishing upon the Throne) and similar verses, explaining that they do not imply physical location. He then shows that attributing place to Allah does not glorify Him; rather, places are glorified by Him. The argument proceeds to refute both the view that Allah is in a specific place (the Throne) and the view that He is everywhere, using the principle that such attributions would either limit Him or fail to properly honor Him. Finally, the passage introduces a new issue (mas'ala) about how to understand divine attributes like essence (mahiya), quality (kayfiyya), and nearness (qurb), emphasizing that these are not to be understood in a physical or spatial sense.

إضافة
تعظيم
تشريف
مكان
أزل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah is everywhere in a literal sense.
Correction: Allah is not in any place, whether specific or general; He is transcendent above place.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi argue that saying Allah is everywhere is as problematic as saying He is in a specific place?
A) Because both imply spatial limitation and change.
B) Because the Qur'an says Allah is on the Throne.
C) Because it contradicts the verse 'We are nearer'.
D) Because it is a form of shirk.

Key Takeaway
Allah is not limited by any place, whether specific or general; He is transcendent, and any spatial attribution is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Allah is with me,' do you ever imagine a spatial nearness? After reading this, how will you correct that notion, and what does true nearness to Allah mean for your daily actions?
?
You have likely heard 'Allah is everywhere' as a comforting thought. But this passage reveals it as a limitation. How does realizing Allah's transcendence over place change the way you seek closeness to Him in your worship?
?
Maturidi says attributions to Allah honor the thing, not Allah. Think of the Kaaba, the Quran, or the Prophet. Do you ever treat these as if they contain Allah's essence? How can you honor them without limiting Allah?

Attribution to God: Honor, Not Location
Maturidi explains the honorific purpose of divine attribution and refutes spatial implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that attributing created things to God, such as the Throne, is for the purpose of honoring them, not for indicating spatial location.

Core Idea
Attribution to God magnifies the created, not confines the Creator.

Maturidi begins by clarifying how we should understand phrases like 'the Throne of God.' In the witnessed world, when we attribute something to God, it is to elevate that thing—not to suggest God is located within it. This lesson unpacks the logic behind this principle and why it protects God's transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Maturidi uses a very compressed style here.
2
Identify the main claim about attribution
Find where Maturidi states the purpose of attributing things to God. Look for the phrase 'يخرج مخرج التعظيم' and understand its significance.
3
Examine the argument against spatial interpretations
Trace how Maturidi refutes those who say God is in every place. Identify the logical steps he uses and the analogy he provides.
This is the core of his argument.
4
Reflect on the examples and ultimate conclusion
Consider the examples of 'Lord of everything' vs 'Lord of Muhammad' and how they illustrate his point. End by understanding God's transcendence above time and space.
Connect this to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يتغير الفهم عن الإضافة عما كان من قبل، وإليه ينصرف الفهم عن الإضافة إلى خلقه. على أن تخصيص إضافات الأشياء إلى الله في الشاهد يخرج مخرج التعظيم لها بما جعل فيها من الأمور المرضية والأحوال المحمودة، فما بال العرش من بين ذلك؟ ولا قوة إلا بالله. وعلى ذلك يفسد قول من يصفه بكل مكان؛ إذ لا فرق بين مكان واحد مخصوص يضاف إليه وبين الجملة. بل الفرد في بيان تعظيمه أولى؛ إذ في ذلك تخصيص ذلك الشيء بالذكر، وفي الذكر تشريف وتكريم؛ فيرجع إلى ذكر علوّ ذلك الشيء. وفي الإرسال وجمع الكل يرجع إلى تخصيص حقيقة صفة الله. كما يقال: رب كل شيء، وإله كل شيء، على تعظيم الرب وتبجيله. وإذا قيل: رب محمد وإله إبراهيم، فإنما يقصد قصد تشريفهما وتعظيمهما. فقياس ذلك أن تكون الإضافة إلى العرش توجب تعظيم العرش وتكريمه، وإلى كل الأمكنة توجب وصف الله بها، وذلك قبيح؛ إذ لم يكن يوصف به في الأزل. ولا يوصف شيء بالقرب إلى الله من طريق المسافة والمساحة ولا هو بالقرب إلى شيء من ذلك الوجه؛ إذ ذلك جهة الحدود والتقدير بالأمكنة؛ وقد كان ولا مكان فهو على ما كان يتعالى عن الزمان والمكان؛ إذ إليهما ترجع حدود الأشياء ونهايتها. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
The understanding of attribution changes from what it was before, and to it the understanding of attribution to His creation turns. However, the specification of the attributions of things to God in the witnessed [world] comes out as a form of magnification for them due to what is placed in them of pleasing matters and praiseworthy states, so what about the Throne among that? And there is no power except with God. And upon that the statement of whoever describes Him with every place becomes invalid, for there is no distinction between one specific place attributed to Him and the whole. Rather, the individual [place] is more deserving in expressing His magnification, for in that there is specification of that thing by mention, and in mention there is honor and veneration, so it returns to the mention of the loftiness of that thing. And in sending [absolutely] and gathering the whole, it returns to the specification of the reality of God's attribute. Just as it is said: Lord of everything and God of everything, for the magnification and veneration of the Lord. And when it is said: Lord of Muhammad and God of Ibrahim, then only the purpose of honoring and magnifying them is intended. So by analogy, attribution to the Throne necessitates magnifying and honoring the Throne, and to all places necessitates describing God by them, and that is ugly, for He was not described by it in pre-eternity. And nothing is described as near to God by way of distance and extent, nor is He near to anything in that respect, for that is the realm of limits and estimation by places; and He was with no place, so He is as He was, exalted above time and space, for to them return the boundaries of things and their ends. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of how attribution (idafa) of things to God should be understood. Maturidi begins by stating that the understanding of attribution changes from what it was before, and the proper understanding turns to attributions to His creation (i.e., the created world). He explains that when we attribute things to God in the witnessed world, it is done to magnify and honor those things because of the pleasing and praiseworthy qualities God placed in them. So when we ask why the Throne is singled out among other things, it is because it is honored. Then he refutes those who say God is in every place: if attributing a specific place to God were taken literally, there would be no difference between one place and all places, and singling out a place for honor would be even more appropriate for magnification. But the point is that mention of something in relation to God is for honor, not location. He gives examples: saying 'Lord of everything' is for magnification, and saying 'Lord of Muhammad' is to honor Muhammad. Similarly, attributing the Throne to God honors the Throne, but attributing all places to God would require describing God by them, which is invalid because God was not described by places in pre-eternity. He then argues that nearness to God is not physical distance or extent, for that implies limits and boundaries. God was without place before creation, so He is now as He was, transcendent above time and space, since boundaries and ends return to them. The passage guards against anthropomorphism and spatializing God.

Key Terms
إضافة (idafa)
تعظيم (ta'zim)
عرش ('arsh)
مكان (makan)
قرب (qurb)
مسافة (masafa)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That attributing a specific place (like the Throne) to God means God is physically located in that place.
Correction: Maturidi clarifies that such attribution is for the honor and magnification of the thing, not to indicate God's location. God transcends all spatial attributes.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the purpose of attributing specific things like the Throne to God?
A) To indicate God's physical location
B) To honor and magnify those things
C) To suggest God is limited to that thing
D) To deny God's transcendence

Key Takeaway
Attribution of things to God is for their honor, not to describe God's location; God transcends space.

When you say 'Lord of the worlds' (Rabb al-'alameen) in your prayer, do you truly intend to magnify God, or do you subconsciously think of Him as being 'in' the worlds? This lesson teaches that such attribution is for honor. Right now, can you repeat that phrase with the correct understanding? Will you make that intention from now on?

But this passage clarifies that singling out the Throne is to honor it, not to locate God. How attached are you to a mental image of God 'sitting' on a throne? Are you willing to let go of that image to preserve God's transcendence? That is a test of your faith in the unseen. What step will you take today to purify your belief?

Understanding the Question 'How' Regarding God
Maturidi analyzes the term 'kayfiyya' into two invalid senses and affirms divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two meanings of 'kayf' (how) when asked about God, and why the only appropriate answer is to affirm God's attributes without comparison.

Core Idea
Asking 'how' about God is either seeking a likeness or asking about modality; both are invalid.

When we ask 'how' about God, we might be seeking a likeness or asking about the modality of His attributes. Maturidi clarifies that both are inappropriate for the transcendent Creator, except that we can affirm He describes Himself with attributes like mercy, knowledge, and power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Maturidi uses a very compressed style here.
2
Distinguish the two meanings
Identify the two aspects of 'kayf' mentioned: seeking an example for God, and asking about the modality of His attribute.
3
Understand the exception
Note the clause about describing God with what He described Himself. This shows that affirming attributes is allowed as long as we do not ask 'how'.
This exception prevents a total denial of attributes.
4
Reflect on the principle
Consider why this teaching protects divine transcendence while allowing meaningful talk about God's attributes.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والكيفية يحتمل وجهين: أحدهما طلب المثال له، أن يكون مثلاً لشيء من الأشياء، والله واحد يجل عن الأشباه. والثاني يحتمل: كيف صفته؟ فجوابه مثل الأول: أن ليس لصفته كيف، إذ هو طلب المثال، وهو يتعالى عن الشبه بالذات والصفة؛ إلا أن يريد به أيوصف هو؟ قيل: بلى، بما وصف به نفسه من الرحمة والعلم والقدرة. وقول القائل: أين هو؟ سؤال عن مكان، وقد بيّنا أنه يتعالى عن ذلك. ولا يوصف الله سبحانه بالاتصال بالأشياء ولا الانفصال، ولا بالحلول فيها ولا بالخروج منها من جهة المسافة على ما هو؛ لأن الله تعالى كان ولا غيره، فمحال انتقاله مما كان عليه بكون غيره لما مر بيانه. وعلى التفسير بالخروج من صفات الخلق وشبهه يجوز. ولا قوة إلا بالله. ويوصف بالقرب من طريق العون والنصر، ومن جهة التشريف والتخصيص، ومن جهة الرحمة والإحسان، ومن جهة التوفيق والإرشاد، ومن جهة هذا النوع؛ لأن وصف هذا كله وصف ذاتي. جائز أن يقال: لم يزل رحيما بأوليائه، محبا لهم لوقت كونهم له أولياء، مبغضا لأعدائه على ذلك. وأما الوجوه التي هي حقيقة تلك الصفات والتي يحققها غيره في الله - لا أنه بذاته يوصف بها - فإنه فاسد؛ لأنه لا يخلو من أن يكون له مدح وتمجيد وتعظيم.
And modality (kayfiyya) carries two aspects: one of them is seeking an example for Him, that He be like something of things, and God is One, exalted above likenesses. The second carries [the meaning]: how is His attribute? So its answer is like the first: that His attribute has no 'how', for it is seeking an example, and He is exalted above similarity in essence and attribute; unless one intends: is He described? It is said: yes, with what He described Himself of mercy, knowledge, and power. And the statement of the one who says: 'Where is He?' is a question about place, and we have explained that He is exalted above that. And God the Glorified is not described with connection (ittisal) to things nor with separation (infisal), nor with indwelling (hulul) in them nor with exit (khuruj) from them by way of distance as it is; because God the Exalted was when nothing else existed, so it is impossible for Him to change from what He was due to the existence of something else, as has passed in its explanation. And upon the interpretation of exiting from the attributes of creation and its like, it is permissible. And there is no power except with God. And He is described with nearness by way of aid (awn) and victory (nasr), and from the direction of honor (tashrif) and specification (takhsis), and from the direction of mercy (rahma) and beneficence (ihsan), and from the direction of success (tawfiq) and guidance (irshad), and from the direction of this type; for the description of all this is a description of essence. It is permissible to say: He has never ceased to be merciful to His friends, loving them for the time of their being His friends, hating His enemies for that. And as for the aspects which are the reality of those attributes and which another realises in God - not that He is described by them in His essence - then it is corrupt, for it cannot be free from having for Him praise, glorification, and magnification.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage is a classification and refutation. Maturidi discusses the question of 'kayf' (how) and 'ayn' (where) regarding God, and concludes with a discussion of nearness (qurb). First, he analyzes 'kayfiyya' (modality) into two meanings: 1) seeking an example or likeness for God – this is invalid because God is one, exalted above any likeness. 2) Asking about the modality of His attribute – the answer is that His attribute has no 'how,' because that would again seek a likeness. However, if one asks 'is He described?' the answer is yes, with attributes He Himself described: mercy, knowledge, power. Second, 'where is He?' is a question about place, and God is exalted above place. Moreover, God cannot be described with connection or separation from things, nor with indwelling or exiting spatially, because God existed when nothing else existed, so it is impossible for Him to change due to the existence of creation. Some interpretations allow speaking of 'exit' metaphorically to negate created attributes. Third, nearness (qurb) to God is not spatial; it is interpreted as aid, victory, honor, specification, mercy, beneficence, success, and guidance – these are descriptions of His essence. It is permissible to say that God has always been merciful to His friends, loving them when they become His friends, and hating His enemies. Finally, Maturidi refutes those who claim that these attributes (like mercy) have a reality that someone else realizes in God, distinct from His essence – this is corrupt because it implies imperfection in God, who is praised, glorified, and magnified.

Key Terms
كيفية (kayfiyya)
مثال (mithal)
شبه (shibh)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Denying 'how' means God has no attributes.
Correction: Maturidi affirms that God is described with the attributes He mentioned, but without modality.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the problem with asking 'how is God's attribute?'
A) It implies seeking a likeness
B) It implies God has no attributes
C) It is a valid question about modality
D) It implies God is in a place

Key Takeaway
The question 'how' about God is either a request for a likeness or an impossible modality; the proper response is to affirm God's self-described attributes without comparison.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God's mercy, do you ever catch yourself imagining it in a human, limited way? What would it take for you to affirm His mercy without forming any mental picture?
?
Have you ever found yourself subtly demanding that God fit into your understanding—asking 'how' about His decisions or attributes? What does this lesson demand you do with that impulse?
?
If someone asked you tomorrow, 'How is God powerful?', how would you answer based on this passage—and how can you train your heart to be content with affirming His attributes without needing a 'how'?

Understanding the Question 'Where' Regarding God
Maturidi rejects spatial questions and attributes regarding God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why asking 'where is God?' is invalid, and that God cannot be described with spatial relations like connection, separation, indwelling, or exit.

Core Idea
God is not in a place, nor connected to or separate from creation.

Some ask 'where is God?' implying a location. Maturidi explains that God is exalted above place and cannot be described with spatial categories such as connection, separation, indwelling, or exit. Because God existed before anything else, He does not change due to creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation to get an overview.
2
Identify the main question
Note that the passage begins by addressing the question 'Where is God?' and declares it invalid.
3
List the rejected spatial attributes
Identify the four terms: connection, separation, indwelling, and exit.
These are all spatial categories.
4
Understand the reason
The reason given: God existed when nothing else existed, so He cannot change due to creation.
5
Note the permissible interpretation
Maturidi allows a metaphorical interpretation of 'exit' as exiting from created attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والكيفية يحتمل وجهين: أحدهما طلب المثال له، أن يكون مثلاً لشيء من الأشياء، والله واحد يجل عن الأشباه. والثاني يحتمل: كيف صفته؟ فجوابه مثل الأول: أن ليس لصفته كيف، إذ هو طلب المثال، وهو يتعالى عن الشبه بالذات والصفة؛ إلا أن يريد به أيوصف هو؟ قيل: بلى، بما وصف به نفسه من الرحمة والعلم والقدرة. وقول القائل: أين هو؟ سؤال عن مكان، وقد بيّنا أنه يتعالى عن ذلك. ولا يوصف الله سبحانه بالاتصال بالأشياء ولا الانفصال، ولا بالحلول فيها ولا بالخروج منها من جهة المسافة على ما هو؛ لأن الله تعالى كان ولا غيره، فمحال انتقاله مما كان عليه بكون غيره لما مر بيانه. وعلى التفسير بالخروج من صفات الخلق وشبهه يجوز. ولا قوة إلا بالله. ويوصف بالقرب من طريق العون والنصر، ومن جهة التشريف والتخصيص، ومن جهة الرحمة والإحسان، ومن جهة التوفيق والإرشاد، ومن جهة هذا النوع؛ لأن وصف هذا كله وصف ذاتي. جائز أن يقال: لم يزل رحيما بأوليائه، محبا لهم لوقت كونهم له أولياء، مبغضا لأعدائه على ذلك. وأما الوجوه التي هي حقيقة تلك الصفات والتي يحققها غيره في الله - لا أنه بذاته يوصف بها - فإنه فاسد؛ لأنه لا يخلو من أن يكون له مدح وتمجيد وتعظيم.
And modality (kayfiyya) carries two aspects: one of them is seeking an example for Him, that He be like something of things, and God is One, exalted above likenesses. The second carries [the meaning]: how is His attribute? So its answer is like the first: that His attribute has no 'how', for it is seeking an example, and He is exalted above similarity in essence and attribute; unless one intends: is He described? It is said: yes, with what He described Himself of mercy, knowledge, and power. And the statement of the one who says: 'Where is He?' is a question about place, and we have explained that He is exalted above that. And God the Glorified is not described with connection (ittisal) to things nor with separation (infisal), nor with indwelling (hulul) in them nor with exit (khuruj) from them by way of distance as it is; because God the Exalted was when nothing else existed, so it is impossible for Him to change from what He was due to the existence of something else, as has passed in its explanation. And upon the interpretation of exiting from the attributes of creation and its like, it is permissible. And there is no power except with God. And He is described with nearness by way of aid (awn) and victory (nasr), and from the direction of honor (tashrif) and specification (takhsis), and from the direction of mercy (rahma) and beneficence (ihsan), and from the direction of success (tawfiq) and guidance (irshad), and from the direction of this type; for the description of all this is a description of essence. It is permissible to say: He has never ceased to be merciful to His friends, loving them for the time of their being His friends, hating His enemies for that. And as for the aspects which are the reality of those attributes and which another realises in God - not that He is described by them in His essence - then it is corrupt, for it cannot be free from having for Him praise, glorification, and magnification.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage is a classification and refutation. Maturidi discusses the question of 'kayf' (how) and 'ayn' (where) regarding God, and concludes with a discussion of nearness (qurb). First, he analyzes 'kayfiyya' (modality) into two meanings: 1) seeking an example or likeness for God – this is invalid because God is one, exalted above any likeness. 2) Asking about the modality of His attribute – the answer is that His attribute has no 'how,' because that would again seek a likeness. However, if one asks 'is He described?' the answer is yes, with attributes He Himself described: mercy, knowledge, power. Second, 'where is He?' is a question about place, and God is exalted above place. Moreover, God cannot be described with connection or separation from things, nor with indwelling or exiting spatially, because God existed when nothing else existed, so it is impossible for Him to change due to the existence of creation. Some interpretations allow speaking of 'exit' metaphorically to negate created attributes. Third, nearness (qurb) to God is not spatial; it is interpreted as aid, victory, honor, specification, mercy, beneficence, success, and guidance – these are descriptions of His essence. It is permissible to say that God has always been merciful to His friends, loving them when they become His friends, and hating His enemies. Finally, Maturidi refutes those who claim that these attributes (like mercy) have a reality that someone else realizes in God, distinct from His essence – this is corrupt because it implies imperfection in God, who is praised, glorified, and magnified.

Key Terms
أين (ayn)
اتصال (ittisal)
انفصال (infisal)
حلول (hulul)
خروج (khuruj)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'where is God?' is a valid question with a literal answer.
Correction: It is invalid because God is beyond place.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why is it impossible for God to change from His state when creation came into being?
A) Because God is unchangeable
B) Because He existed when nothing else existed
C) Because He is omnipotent
D) Because He is in a place

Key Takeaway
God is not in a place nor subject to spatial relationships; He was before all things and does not change.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray, do you find yourself unconsciously directing your heart to a specific place (e.g., the sky, the Kaaba) as if God is there? How can you train your soul to believe that He is not in any place, yet He hears your every word?
?
If you have ever felt that God 'enters' your heart or 'dwells' in a mosque, what correction does this lesson demand of you? Are you willing to abandon such imagery even if it feels comforting?
?
The passage says God was when nothing else existed. Reflect: Has your reliance on creation (people, possessions, status) ever overshadowed your reliance on the Creator alone? What concrete change will you make today to shift that reliance back to Him?

Understanding Nearness to God
Maturidi interprets divine nearness metaphorically and refutes a corrupt view of attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that nearness to God is not physical but metaphorical, and that interpretations claiming a separate reality for divine attributes are corrupt.

Core Idea
Nearness to God means aid, honor, mercy, and guidance—not physical closeness.

The term 'nearness' (qurb) is often misunderstood literally. Maturidi explains that nearness to God is interpreted as His aid, victory, honor, mercy, beneficence, success, and guidance. These are descriptions of His essence. He then refutes those who claim that these attributes have a reality realized by another in God, which would imply imperfection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully.
2
Identify the meanings of nearness
List the five ways Maturidi interprets nearness: aid, victory, honor, mercy, guidance, etc.
3
Understand the essence connection
Note that these are described as 'descriptions of essence' (wasf dhati).
4
Analyze the refutation
Identify the corrupt view: that these attributes have a reality distinct from God's essence, realized by another.
5
Reflect on the principle
Consider why this refutation is important for affirming God's perfection and praise.

Source Text

And modality (kayfiyya) carries two aspects: one of them is seeking an example for Him, that He be like something of things, and God is One, exalted above likenesses. The second carries [the meaning]: how is His attribute? So its answer is like the first: that His attribute has no 'how', for it is seeking an example, and He is exalted above similarity in essence and attribute; unless one intends: is He described? The Meaning of 'How' About God
Explains the two aspects of the question 'how' about God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two meanings of the question 'how' (kayf) when asked about God, and why only self-description is permissible.

Core Idea
Asking 'How is God?' either seeks a likeness or asks about attributes—both must be answered without comparison.

This passage from Imam Maturidi addresses a common question about divine attributes. When someone asks 'how' about God, it can mean two very different things. The author clarifies each meaning and explains how a Muslim should respond.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two meanings of kayf
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice that 'kayf' can mean either seeking a likeness for God or asking about His attributes.
The second meaning is often mistaken as similar to asking about created things.
2
Understand why each meaning is answered similarly
Both meanings ultimately lead to the conclusion that God's essence and attributes have no 'how' because they are beyond comparison.
3
Note the exception for self-description
The only permissible way to describe God is by what He has described Himself, such as mercy, knowledge, and power.
This avoids falling into anthropomorphism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و [ السؤال عن ] الكيفية يحتمل وجهين: أحدهما طلب المثال له، أن يكون مثلاً لشيء من الأشياء ؛ والله واحد يجل عن الأشباه. و [ثانيهما] يحتمل : كيف صفته ؟ فجوابه : مثل الأول أن ليس لصفته كيف، إذ هو طلب المثال ، وهو يتعالى عن الشبه بالذات والصفة؛ إلا أن يريد به أيوصف هو ؟ قيل: بلى، بما وصف به نفسه من الرحمة والعلم والقدرة. وقول القائل : أين هو ؟ سؤال عن مكان، وقد بيّنا أنه يتعالى عن ذلك. ولا يوصف الله سبحانه بالاتصال بالأشياء ولا الانفصال، ولا بالحلول فيها ولا بالخروج منها من جهة المسافة على ما هو ؛ لأن الله تعالى كان ولا غيره، فمحال انتقاله مما كان عليه بكون غيره لما مر بيانه. وعلى التفسير بالخروج من صفات الخلق وشبهه يجوز. ويوصف بالقرب من طريق العون والنصر، ومن جهة التشريف والتخصيص، ومن جهة الرحمة والإحسان، ومن جهة التوفيق والإرشاد، و [ من جهة ] هذا النوع؛ لأن وصف هذا كله وصف ذاتي. جائز أن يقال : لم يزل رحيما بأوليائه، محبا لهم لوقت كونهم له أولياء، مبغضا لأعدائه على ذلك.
And [the question about] the 'how' (kayfiyya) admits two aspects: one is seeking a likeness for Him, that He be similar to something among things — but God is One, exalted above likenesses. And [the second] admits: 'How is His attribute?' So its answer is like the first, that His attribute has no 'how', because it is seeking a likeness, and He is exalted above similarity in essence and attribute. Unless one means by it 'Is He described?' It is said: Yes, by what He described Himself with: mercy, knowledge, and power. And the statement of the questioner: 'Where is He?' is a question about place, and we have explained that He is exalted above that. And God, glorified, is not described by connection with things nor disconnection, nor by indwelling in them nor by exiting from them in terms of distance as it is; because God existed and nothing else existed, so it is impossible for Him to change from what He was by the existence of something else, as has been explained. And according to the interpretation of 'exit' from the attributes of creation and their likeness, it is permissible. And He is described with nearness (qurb) by way of help and victory, and in terms of honor and specification, and in terms of mercy and beneficence, and in terms of success and guidance, and [in terms of] this type; because the description of all this is a description of the essence. It is permissible to say: He has always been merciful to His friends, loving them at the time they become His friends, hating His enemies accordingly.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage addresses two types of questions about God: 'how' (kayf) and 'where' (ayn). For 'how', the author explains that it has two meanings: either asking for a likeness (which is impossible for God) or asking about the nature of His attributes (which also have no 'how' because they are unlike created attributes). The only permissible way to describe God is by what He has described Himself. For 'where', the author states that God is exalted above place; He is not connected or disconnected from things, nor does He dwell in them or exit them in a spatial sense. However, He is described with nearness (qurb) in terms of help, honor, mercy, and guidance—these are real descriptions of His essence. This nearness is not spatial but relational.

Key Terms
الكيفية
المثال
الصفة
الأشباه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One can ask 'how' about God's attributes in the same way as asking about created things.
Correction: God's attributes are unique and have no 'how'; we can only describe them by God's own self-description.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the first meaning of the question 'how' regarding God?
A) Asking about God's location
B) Seeking a likeness for God
C) Asking about God's actions
D) Asking about God's essence

Key Takeaway
The question 'how' about God either seeks a likeness or asks about attributes, and both are answered by affirming divine transcendence and relying on God's self-description.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you catch yourself trying to imagine or picture God's mercy in your mind, what temptation are you falling into that this lesson exposes? What will you do the next time you sense that impulse?
?
Is there an attribute of God that you feel you can 'understand' fully? How does this passage challenge that feeling, and what would it mean for you to accept that you cannot know the 'how'?
?
Reflect on a time you felt you needed to explain God's actions or attributes to someone in a way that made them seem like a created thing. What would it look like to simply affirm God's description without adding a 'how'?
